## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear dynamics of oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), indicating a second-order ODE written in first-order form for an oscillator. Nonlinear harmonic oscillator models typically express dv_dt as a restoring force term in x plus damping terms in v, optionally with nonlinear stiffness, nonlinear damping, and time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, no damping/forcing)
- Linear viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper)
- Constant or bias acceleration: dv_dt = c0 - c1 * x - c2 * v (equilibrium shift / constant forcing)
- Sinusoidal external forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driven damped oscillator)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x - c4 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order polynomial stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (multi-well or strong nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping)
- Nonlinear damping with amplitude dependence: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent negative damping at small |v|)
- Pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle restoring torque with viscous damping)
- Energy-conserving nonlinear potential (general): dv_dt = -c0 * d_dx_U(x) - c1 * v, with d_dx_U(x) ≈ c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (conservative force from a potential plus damping, approximated by polynomial)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator behavior → dv_dt primarily a function of x (no explicit v or t), often an odd function of x for symmetric potentials (e.g., -x, -x - x**3).
- Linear viscous damping → additive term proportional to -v; causes exponential decay of oscillation amplitude without changing equilibrium position.
- Quadratic/velocity-magnitude drag → terms like -v*Abs(v); stronger damping at high speeds and sharper decay for large-amplitude motion.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles → negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, typically via (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness → sign of the x**3 term: +x**3 increases frequency with amplitude (hardening), -x**3 decreases it (softening).
- Parametric resonance → stiffness multiplied by periodic functions of t, e.g., cos(c*t)*x; yields instability tongues near specific modulation frequencies.
- External periodic forcing → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; can produce resonance peaks, beats, and phase locking depending on damping.
- Geometric nonlinear restoring force → sin(c*x) (pendulum-like) implies bounded restoring force at large |x| and amplitude-dependent period.

GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x
Candidate formulas: 269

GT (fixed) is
\[
0.2660689198\sin(t)\;-\;0.4334248932\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;3.056411937\,x\big(0.08255811776|v|^{1/3}+1\big).
\]
Expand key structure:
- Sinusoid term: \(+0.2660\sin(t)\) (depends only on \(t\), not on \(x\) or \(v\)).
- Damping-like polynomial term: \(-0.4334\,v + 0.4334\,v x^2\) (has a \(v x^2\) cross-term).
- Stiffness/friction term: \(-3.0564\,x - (3.0564\cdot 0.0825581)\,x|v|^{1/3}\).
So GT contains **both** cross-terms \(v x^2\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\), and also a **pure** \(\sin(t)\) term.

Now check candidates for whether they can reproduce *all* these dependencies by choosing constants.

1. \(c0x+c1v+c2v|v|+c3 e^{c4|t|}\sin(c5 t+c6)\): has \(x\), \(v\), \(v|v|\), and a time sinusoid possibly with exponential envelope. **Missing** \(vx^2\) and **missing** \(x|v|^{1/3}\). No way to create those cross-terms. Not match.

2. \(c0x+c1x^3+c2v+c3\cos(c4 t+c5)\): has \(x,x^3,v,\cos(t)\). **Missing** \(vx^2\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

3. \(c0x+c1v+c2 e^{c3|t|}\sin(c4 t+c5)\): only linear \(x,v\) plus time sinusoid. **Missing** \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

4. \(c0x+c1v+c2v|v|+c3\sin(c4x+c5)\cos(c6t+c7)\): introduces \(x\)-dependent trig product, but GT has no trig in \(x\). Also still **no** \(vx^2\) or \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

5. \(c0v+c1x+c2v^3+c3 x/(c4 t+c5)+c6/(c4 t+c5)\): rational-in-\(t\) terms not in GT; has \(v^3\) not in GT; **missing** \(\sin(t)\), \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

6. \(c0v+c1x+c2v^3+c3 x(c4+t)^{c5}\): time-power coupling to \(x\) not in GT; **missing** \(\sin(t)\) (pure), \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

7. \(c0x+c1v+c2v|v|+c3 x/(c4 t+c5)+c6/(c4 t+c5)\): has \(v|v|\) and rational-in-\(t\); GT has neither. **Missing** \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\), and pure \(\sin(t)\). Not match.

8. \(c0x+c1v+c2 x\cos(c3 t+c4)+c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\): can match the pure \(\sin(t)\) term by setting \(c6=1\), phase \(c7=0\), \(c5=0.2660\). But it also has an \(x\cos(\cdot)\) term; to remove it set \(c2=0\). Then it reduces to linear \(x,v\) plus \(\sin(t)\). Still **missing** \(vx^2\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

9. \(c0x+c1v+c2v|v|+c3 x(c4+t)^{c5}\): no \(\sin(t)\) unless via weird choices (not possible); **missing** \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

10. \(c0x+c1v+c2 + c3 x\cos(c4 t+c5)+ c6 v x^2\): This one can produce the **\(v x^2\)** term via \(c6 v x^2\). It can also produce linear \(x\) and linear \(v\). However:
- GT needs a **pure** \(\sin(t)\) term; candidate has only \(x\cos(\cdot)\) time dependence, not a standalone \(\sin(t)\). Setting \(c3=0\) removes time dependence entirely; keeping \(c3\neq 0\) makes time dependence multiplied by \(x\), which GT does not have.
- GT also needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\), which candidate cannot form (no \(|v|^{1/3}\)).
So cannot match.

11. \(c0x+c1x^3+c2v+c3 x(c4+t)^{c5}\): no \(\sin(t)\), no \(vx^2\), no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

12. \(c0x+c1v+c2 x/(c3 t+c4)+c5/(c3 t+c4)\): rational-in-\(t\) not in GT; no \(\sin(t)\), no \(vx^2\), no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

13. \(c0x+c1v+c2x+c3 t x+c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\): can match \(\sin(t)\) (set \(c5=1,c6=0,c4=0.2660\)) and combine \(c0x+c2x\) into linear \(x\). But it has \(t x\) unless \(c3=0\). After removing \(tx\), still only linear \(x,v\) plus \(\sin(t)\): **missing** \(vx^2\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

14. \(c0 + c1v + c2 x\cos(c3 t+c4)+ c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\): can match \(\sin(t)\) by phase/frequency choice, and set \(c2=0\) to remove \(x\cos\). Then only constant + linear \(v\) + \(\sin(t)\): **missing** \(x\), \(vx^2\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

15–269 (general pattern check): GT requires simultaneously:
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (not multiplied by \(x\) or \(v\)),
- a \(v x^2\) term,
- an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term with a fractional power and absolute value,
- plus linear \(x\) and linear \(v\).

Scan the list for any candidate containing **both** (i) a standalone \(\sin(\text{affine in }t)\) term and (ii) a term of the form \(v x^2\) and (iii) a term involving \(|v|^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(x\).
- Many candidates include \(\sin(\cdot)\) in \(t\) (e.g., 8, 13, 36, 49, 82, 92, 96, 100, 112, 114, 117, 125, 134, 139, 193, 194, 198, 199, 209, 210, 217, 223, 231, 246, 247, etc.), but none of these include an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term.
- Candidates that include \(v x^2\) (e.g., 10 has \(c6 v x^2\); 75/76 have \(v x^2\); 101/102/104/105/108/109/112/114/137 etc. have \(v x^2\) or similar) do not include \(|v|^{1/3}\) and typically lack a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (some have \(\sin(t)\) but still no \(|v|^{1/3}\)).
- Candidates that include \(\mathrm{Abs}(v)\) appear mostly as \(v|v|\), \(\log(\cdot|v|+1)\), or \(|v|^{c}\) but **none** provide the specific fractional power \(|v|^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(x\) in an additive way matching GT. The only forms with \(\mathrm{Abs}(v)^{c}\) are like #131: \(c3|v|^{c4}|x|^{c5\!}\) (but that uses \(|x|\) and lacks \(\sin(t)\) and \(vx^2\)); and various log/exp constructions that cannot simplify to a plain \(|v|^{1/3}\) term for all real \(v\).
- Candidates with \(v|v|\) cannot be made equal to \(x|v|^{1/3}\) or to \(v x^2\) by parameter choice because the functional dependence on \(v\) (power 2 vs 1/3) and on \(x\) (none vs \(x\) vs \(x^2\)) is fundamentally different, and absolute values cannot be dropped under the strict sign-changing domain.

Also, no candidate includes the exact combination \(-a v(1-x^2)\) which requires both \(v\) and \(v x^2\) with tied coefficients (same magnitude, opposite sign). Some candidates can include both \(v\) and \(v x^2\) (e.g., 114, 101), but they still cannot produce the \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term, and they generally cannot produce a pure \(\sin(t)\) term simultaneously in the right additive form without extra unwanted terms.

Therefore, there is **no** candidate whose parameterization can reproduce all three essential GT features (pure \(\sin(t)\), \(v x^2\), and \(x|v|^{1/3}\)) over a sign-changing domain.

[NO MATCH]

2. `v` (linear in v)
3. `v*x**2` (v times x squared)
4. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` (x times cube root of |v|)
5. `sin(t)`

This is a very specific combination. Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce ALL five terms.

Key observations:
- Terms 3 and 4 involve products of x and functions of v, which are quite specific
- The `x*|v|^(1/3)` term is particularly distinctive
- Most candidates won't have the right basis functions

Let me systematically check candidates. I'll focus on whether candidates can produce all required basis functions.

Most candidates lack `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` and/or `v*x**2` and/or `sin(t)`. Let me check the ones that might work:

**Candidates with `v*x**2`:** 75, 76, 84, 98, 101, 102, 104, 105, 108, 109, 112, 114, 119, 200, 201

None of these also have `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` and `sin(t)`.

**Candidates with `x*|v|^(1/3)` equivalent:** None explicitly have this term.

Since the GT requires the term `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`, which is a very specific nonlinear coupling between x and v, essentially no candidate can produce this unless it has a sufficiently flexible functional form.

Let me check candidates with general power terms like `x*(c4 + v)**c5` or `v*(c4 + x)**c5`:
- These expand differently and can't isolate `x*|v|^(1/3)` exactly.

Candidate 25 (rational in x with v terms) and 51 (rational in v with x terms) and 236 could potentially be flexible but still can't produce `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

Candidate 251: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**c3` - missing v*x² and sin(t) and x*|v|^(1/3).

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the basis function `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` (or equivalently `x*|v|^(1/3)`), which is essential in the GT. No combination of the available terms in any candidate can reproduce this term exactly.

Let me verify there isn't a candidate I missed with something like `Abs(v)**c` multiplied by x... Candidates 131, 133 have `Abs(v)` with powers but not multiplied by x in the right way, or missing other terms.

Candidate 131: `c0*v + c1*x + c2*v**3 + c3*Abs(v)**c4*Abs(x)**c5` - This gives `|v|^c4 * |x|^c5`, not `x*|v|^(1/3)` since `|x|` ≠ `x`.
